  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_47975a29-7492-4f33-a1e2-349286717771'
      });

"Hope for the Flowers" is an inspiring allegory about the realization of one's true destiny as told through the lives of caterpillars Stripe and Yellow, who struggle to "climb to the top" before understanding that they are meant to fly.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/495862552" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495862552?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780809101740" href="/book/show/2310870.Hope_for_the_Flowers">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495862552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4268878922141667186">Hope for the Flowers, Trina Paulus<br/><br/>It all starts when Stripe, the main character, first hatches from an egg. He begins his life by eating the leaf he was born on. He realizes that there must be "more" to life than just eating leaves. He senses there must be a way to get up into the sky. He searches for a way and finds himself at the base of a pillar made up of caterpillars. <br/><br/>They are all struggling to get up into the sky as well. Here he meets Yellow who also wants to get up into the sky by climbi</span>
  <span id="freeText4268878922141667186" style="display:none">Hope for the Flowers, Trina Paulus<br /><br />It all starts when Stripe, the main character, first hatches from an egg. He begins his life by eating the leaf he was born on. He realizes that there must be "more" to life than just eating leaves. He senses there must be a way to get up into the sky. He searches for a way and finds himself at the base of a pillar made up of caterpillars. <br /><br />They are all struggling to get up into the sky as well. Here he meets Yellow who also wants to get up into the sky by climbing to the top of the pillar. But she feels bad about what must be done to achieve this goal. You have to literally step on and climb over all the other caterpillars who are also trying to reach the top of the pillar. <br /><br />The two of them eventually decide to stop climbing and go back down the pillar. They live together for a while. But Stripe's curiosity and unrest overcome him and he decides that he must get to the top of the pillar. Stripe says good-bye to Yellow. He focuses, adapts, and drives to reach the top, and eventually he succeeds at being on the top of the caterpillar pillar. This results in disillusionment, as he takes in a vast vista of other caterpillar pillars. Is this all there is at the top? He has not really gotten in to the sky. <br /><br />He just has a view of other caterpillars struggling to reach the top of their respective caterpillar pillars. Yellow, however, has followed her instincts, continues to eat and then spins a cocoon. She eventually emerges from the cocoon transformed into a butterfly and flies into the sky effortlessly. She has found the real answer to the feeling that there must be more to life than eating leaves, and who caterpillars really are. She is waiting for the disillusioned Stripe as he descends the pillar and eventually reaches the ground again. She shows Stripe her empty cocoon, and he eventually realizes what he needs to do. Stripe makes a cocoon of his own. Yellow waits for him. Stripe emerges transformed into a butterfly, and they fly off together.<br /><br />عنوانها: «در تکاپوی معنا»؛ «به گل نشستن»؛ «چیزی بیشتر از زندگی: در تکاپوی معنا»؛ نویسنده: ت‍ری‍ن‍ا پ‍الاس‌؛ تاریخ خوانش سال 1987میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: در تکاپوی معنا؛ نویسنده: ت‍ری‍ن‍ا پ‍الاس‌؛ مت‍رج‍م طی‍ب‍ه‌ زن‍دی‌پ‍ور؛ ت‍ه‍ران‌: ف‍ردوس‌، 1366؛ در 148ص؛ چاپ دوم تهران، نشر میترا، 1378؛ در 160ص، مصور؛ رنگی؛ شابک 9645998077؛ چاپ سوم 1381؛ چاپ چهارم 1383؛ چاپ پنجم 1386؛ شابک 9789645998071؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، دیدگاه، 1381؛ در 158ص؛ شابک 9646107222؛ موضوع: داستانهای کوتاه از نویسندگان ایالات متحده آمریکا - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: به گل نشستن؛ نویسنده: ترینا پالاس؛ مترجم موسی نامی؛ تصویرسازی امیر‌محمد جوادی؛ تهران، پژوهه، 1388؛ در 100ص؛ مصور؛ شابک 9789647772754؛<br /><br />عنوان: چیزی بیشتر از زندگی: در تکاپوی معنا؛ نویسنده و تصویرساز ترینا پالوس؛ مترجم زهره زاهدی؛ تهران، پندار تابان، 1397؛ در 160ص؛ مصور؛ شابک 9786008593348؛<br /><br />حکایت زندگی یک «کرم» کوچک «پروانه» است، که سر از تخم درآورده، و به دنبال چیستی زندگی و شناخت خویش، از درختی که در شاخه ‌ی آن زندگی و از برگ‌هایش تغذیه می‌کرده، پایین می‌آید؛ این کرم پروانه که «راه راه» نام دارد، به این نتیجه می‌رسد که زندگی ارزشی بیش از فقط خوردن و بزرگ‌تر شدن دارد…؛ اما ارزش زندگی را چگونه می‌توان پیدا کرد؟<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 06/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_42519821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42519821" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10378-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293990882p2/10378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42519821?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/10378-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">David, Brian, Mark, other misanthropes</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jason by: </span>
      an ex
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42519821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2458493767632600865">A girlfriend gave me this book once. <br/><br/>At the time, I was living on an island of about two hundred people, teaching English. A foolish, miserable task--the kind of "good-for-you" intervention bound up in so many good intentions that the inevitable crass exploitation and inadequate resourcing and nonexistent long-term vision and full-on horseshit stupidity seem, in hindsight, a necessary cosmic counter-balancing. Ostensibly, I was teaching English and helping the other English teachers improve curr</span>
  <span id="freeText2458493767632600865" style="display:none">A girlfriend gave me this book once. <br /><br />At the time, I was living on an island of about two hundred people, teaching English. A foolish, miserable task--the kind of "good-for-you" intervention bound up in so many good intentions that the inevitable crass exploitation and inadequate resourcing and nonexistent long-term vision and full-on horseshit stupidity seem, in hindsight, a necessary cosmic counter-balancing. Ostensibly, I was teaching English and helping the other English teachers improve curriculum. Instead, the other English teachers wised up--let the fucking American handle this shit, and let's hit the lagoon, while the fishing is fine--and I struggled to piece together an elementary curriculum for non-English speakers who'd never heard anyone fluent in English speak. No television, except when the local generator was fired up, and the vhs hooked in, so that we could watch "Best of the Best" and "Best of the Best 2" for a quarter. Two or three radios, which only got Armed Forces Network. One communication radio, intermittently functioning, which I got on once a week to talk to pals distributed around the islands over 40,000 some square miles. I got mail once a week, if the plane showed up, if the weather was good, if I actually got any mail. I could run around the island, by which I mean quite literally I could run around the island. We periodically hit a dry patch where few fish came in, and breadfruit weren't in season, so we ate canned food and rice and coconuts, and when the canned food ran out we ate rice and coconuts. I lost about 60 pounds. I sank into periodic depressions. I certainly got along with everyone, and drank tons of instant coffee hanging out with the guys, but I wasn't really connecting -- except with one guy, a really great person who I was starting to become good friends with, and then he died of tuberculosis. Those periods of depression became more like exclamation points.<br /><br />Twice a year, during the two years I was there, I got into the "main island." (Let's describe that in some other post.) During those trips, I drank excessively. Took up smoking despite having never had any interest in smoking (even leaping straight to Kool Menthols, 'cause as I believe Denis Leary put it if you inhale excessively on a Menthol it feels like your eyes are bleeding). Stayed out to all hours. Fell in love with everyone I met. And at the end of one stay, I began dating (okay, let's call it "dating" as well as dating) a very nice, sweet, good-intentioned English teacher like myself. We had a whirlwind of hyperbolic romantic passion, before we both headed to our respective islands. <br /><br />Months passed. Mail, infrequent, the occasional too-public radio conversation. I had been there... oh, maybe 18 months. I was seriously losing it. And I wrote this sweet, wonderful, well-intentioned woman a cri de coeur, a howl of anguish and existential fear and self-loathing ... and she sent me this book. Oh, she also sent me a very moving, sweet, well-intentioned letter, explaining what the book meant, and how it might help me. She really was a great person. But I read this book and wanted to immediately begin gassing hippies. I turned from self-loathing into a fairly aggressive other-loather. I realized that this task I'd taken on really wasn't for me. A couple weeks later, I left the island and the gig, for good.<br /><br />We broke up, too. I wasn't even sure how to say anything ... the book flabbergasted me. But, in a way, I guess, it saved me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2458493767632600865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12780515820022188200">Someone's comment just reminded me of this one...<br/><br/>I read this when I was a kid (significantly under 10) at the public library.<br/><br/>An allegorical hippie story encouraging people (or caterpillars) to get out of the rat race.   <span id="freeText12780515820022188200" style="display:none">Someone's comment just reminded me of this one...<br /><br />I read this when I was a kid (significantly under 10) at the public library.<br /><br />An allegorical hippie story encouraging people (or caterpillars) to get out of the rat race. I got the allegory, even as a kid. (It's pretty impossible to miss.) Even then, while I didn't disagree with the 'go your own way' part of the message, I thought the delivery was a Bit Much.<br /><br />It features a HORRIFYING scene where the ambitious caterpillars are literally forming pillars, climbing over each other and crushing each other on the way to the top - where they simply fall from the pinnacle to their splatty deaths.<br />I think it scarred me for life.<br /><br />________<br /><br />Another review just mentioned a bit I didn't remember, so I looked it up. Yes, this quote is in there:<br /><br />“Once you are a butterfly,<br />you can really love – the<br />kind of love that makes a<br />new life. It’s better than all<br />the hugging caterpillars can<br />do.” <br /><br />Child-me read that uncritically. Adult-me does not.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6402039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18377298956054226779">this book is written like a childrens book, but for adults. Very reminicent of Esops fables....<br/><br/>I first read it back in high school, a friend saw me looking it over, and then went back and bought it for me. Its very touching....<br/><br/>Its about one catapillar who, unlike the others, isnt happy just eating leaves and climbing the catapillar-pillar. He stops to wonder "why".... he questions everything around him. <br/><br/>Its a little about love, and growing into your own skin, its about doing what has to be done,</span>
  <span id="freeText18377298956054226779" style="display:none">this book is written like a childrens book, but for adults. Very reminicent of Esops fables....<br /><br />I first read it back in high school, a friend saw me looking it over, and then went back and bought it for me. Its very touching....<br /><br />Its about one catapillar who, unlike the others, isnt happy just eating leaves and climbing the catapillar-pillar. He stops to wonder "why".... he questions everything around him. <br /><br />Its a little about love, and growing into your own skin, its about doing what has to be done, but knowing and understanding why its done, rather than doing just for the sake of doing. Its about taking leap of faith, looking around you and knowing there is something more.....<br /><br />I reread it as time passes, just to remind myself of its beauty...</span>
  <a data-text-id="18377298956054226779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/303978-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7879282?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/303978-tom">Tom</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7879282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18118256898582363532">Hope for the Flowers presents a wonderful, charming tale of two caterpillars (Stripe and Yellow) trying to get to the top.<br/><br/>Beguiled at first by a misguided attempt to climb on the heads of their fellow caterpillars (who have commingled into an enormous "caterpillar pillar" that ascends into the sky), Yellow and Stripe eventually abandon the pillar for the simple lives of eating and rolling around on the ground. But Stripe can't contain his curiosity about the pillar, and abandons Yellow to try th</span>
  <span id="freeText18118256898582363532" style="display:none">Hope for the Flowers presents a wonderful, charming tale of two caterpillars (Stripe and Yellow) trying to get to the top.<br /><br />Beguiled at first by a misguided attempt to climb on the heads of their fellow caterpillars (who have commingled into an enormous "caterpillar pillar" that ascends into the sky), Yellow and Stripe eventually abandon the pillar for the simple lives of eating and rolling around on the ground. But Stripe can't contain his curiosity about the pillar, and abandons Yellow to try the climb again. <br /><br />Eventually, he realizes that there is nothing worth having at the top of the pillar, and then begins a search for her and his life's true course in earnest.<br /><br />This book presents an excellent metaphor for adults who feel somehow trapped in the pointless climb to the top of a pillar that leads nowhere, and a cautionary, illuminating tale for children who have not yet been tricked into believing that the only way to get to the top is to step on others to get there. Indeed, the only way to get to the top is to fly, and the way to fly is simple - be true to yourself and be true to your love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18118256898582363532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2091230600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091230600" />
    <a title="Zenki the Hermit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15656397-zenki-the-hermit"><img alt="Zenki the Hermit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522599159p2/15656397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2091230600?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zenki the Hermit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zenki the Hermit" href="/user/show/15656397-zenki-the-hermit">Zenki the Hermit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091230600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10662555883562082015"><b>It's a story about love and ambition.</b><br/><br/>Stripe does not truly know what he wants. All he knows is that he's done with the very monotonous days of seemingly perpetual crawling and leaf-eating. When he sees a lot of <br/>caterpillars climbing towards the clouds, he decides to climb with them, even if he did not <br/>know where he was going. All he knew was that everyone else was going that way, trying to <br/>attain whatever it is at the top, and since everyone seemed to want it, he became convinced <br/>that he wanted </span>
  <span id="freeText10662555883562082015" style="display:none"><b>It's a story about love and ambition.</b><br /><br />Stripe does not truly know what he wants. All he knows is that he's done with the very monotonous days of seemingly perpetual crawling and leaf-eating. When he sees a lot of <br />caterpillars climbing towards the clouds, he decides to climb with them, even if he did not <br />know where he was going. All he knew was that everyone else was going that way, trying to <br />attain whatever it is at the top, and since everyone seemed to want it, he became convinced <br />that he wanted it, too.<br /><br />I found this completely relatable. Even if I had plans of my own, I honestly, sincerely <br />don't really know what I want, where I want to go, and who I'm supposed to be. My goals were <br />very general, like Stripe - keep climbing and hope for the best, keep climbing as long as <br />you're leaving the dull life behind, follow the crowd, if the popular public moves towards a <br />certain area then it must be the best area. And what's sad about this kind of living, this <br />kind of discovering and moving forward, is that it's usually very self-centered. Stripe did not care <br />at all on who he stepped on, on who he hurt just to be a step forward from the rest.<br /><br /><i>Then he met Yellow.</i> Yellow who changes his perspectives, who shared his doubts whether the uncertainty that awaits them is worth it. Yellow who he soon grows to love. They lived a <br />peaceful life together and they were happy for a while but Stripe's curiosity was too <br />obstinate and it made him restless. When it came down to choosing between ambition and <br />settling down with Yellow, Stripe decided to yet again climb the mountain of caterpillars.<br /><br /><b>It's about life.</b><br />Existence, perhaps the greatest enigma of all. And with existence blooms a desire for <br />purpose. Purpose, a certainty any person would want to colorfully paint. No one wants to <br />traverse life insipidly; life should be lived with passion, adventure, and questioning.<br /><br /><b>It's about revolution.</b><br />Sometimes the norm is nothing - cruelly pointless and a thief. And when the majority adhere <br />to these norms, majorities even, it takes a brave soul to break away, an even braver one to <br />save and plead to others to break away. <br /><br /><b>It's about hope.</b><br />Even when Yellow wanted to reach the top of the pile as well, and even if it hurt to admit <br />that she couldn't think of any other way to go up, and even when she loved Stripe so much <br />she wanted to follow him, she stood her ground knowing climbing was the wrong way - if she <br />climbed she'd have to step all over the others all over again. And when Stripe left her for <br />the pile, the waiting overwhelmed her, because she did not want to wait, she searched.<br /><br />OH THERE'S SO MUCH TO GLEAN FROM THIS STORY. I AM SO GLAD TO HAVE ENCOUNTERED IT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10662555883562082015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17483101" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17483101" />
    <a title="booklady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/350218-booklady"><img alt="booklady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591723471p2/350218.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17483101?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booklady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booklady" href="/user/show/350218-booklady">booklady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone any age</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=all-ages">all-ages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=1990s">1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=worth-reading-over-and-over">worth-reading-over-and-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=young-children">young-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=youth">youth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=1970s">1970s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=1980s">1980s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17483101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3415384870332819340">I have loved this book ever since high school when a very special friend shared it with me. It’s been a long time since I read it, but it never fails to charm.<br/><br/>Recently I went on a hunt for it in this jungle house of books, but without success. I know I have a ratty old paperback copy somewhere but I can’t find it. So I checked it out from the library and read it again with profound enjoyment and peace.<br/><br/>It’s that kind of book—a peaceful book. It’s a book which reminds us that we are all so much mo</span>
  <span id="freeText3415384870332819340" style="display:none">I have loved this book ever since high school when a very special friend shared it with me. It’s been a long time since I read it, but it never fails to charm.<br /><br />Recently I went on a hunt for it in this jungle house of books, but without success. I know I have a ratty old paperback copy somewhere but I can’t find it. So I checked it out from the library and read it again with profound enjoyment and peace.<br /><br />It’s that kind of book—a peaceful book. It’s a book which reminds us that we are all so much more than our lowest crawling, grasping, combative work-a-day world might have us believe we are. And so is life.<br /><br />Now my children are teenagers and their attitudes are beginning to sour a bit due to the competitive behavior they see exhibited by their fellow human beings—outside their immediate circle of friends that is. As I listened to the first creeping tones of disillusionment in my eldest daughter’s conversation the other day I realized it was time for this book.<br /><br />Hope for the Flowers is a fable. It reads like a young children’s book with tri-color (black, white and yellow) illustrations. It’s about a caterpillar, Stripe, who is trying to figure out what the world is all about. In the course of his journey he discovers a tower of caterpillars where everyone is climbing over everyone else to get to the top—a top lost in the clouds. What exactly exists at the top and why they are trying to get there remains a mystery to Stripe as well as to his fellow climbers. Nevertheless, Stripe jumps onto the caterpillar pile and starts climbing.<br /><br />Along the way he avoids looking into the eyes of any of the others he steps on or climbs over, but he eventually meets and converses with another caterpillar named Yellow and as a result of this, both of their journeys are forever changed.<br /><br />Don’t want to spoil the story for any who haven’t read it. If you haven’t, you are in for a treat! By all means rush out right now, get yourself a copy and read it! It’s a great winter read. It’s an all-time classic. It’s up-lifting. It’s a book to read over and over and over! This reminds me why I checked it out from the library—to give it to my daughter to read; I’m off to give it to her before it’s due back. Enjoy!<br /><br />*****<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://the--book--nook.blogspot.com/2008/01/hope-for-flowers.html">http://the--book--nook.blogspot.com/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3415384870332819340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_22875140" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22875140" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65207-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465962504p2/65207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22875140?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2008</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6078860237451665106">This allegory coudln't be more unsubtle. Unless at the end the author was like "and like, the caterpillars, are actually like, PEOPLE. And the strive to the top is like, our struggle in life. And like, being a butterfly is..." etc. The illustrations were cutesie pie though. This is such a hippie book I don't even know what else to say. It's hard to hate on such cheesy idealism.... I felt like I should be more impressed by the cute, universal message, than I was. Maybe it'd help if I was less cyn</span>
  <span id="freeText6078860237451665106" style="display:none">This allegory coudln't be more unsubtle. Unless at the end the author was like "and like, the caterpillars, are actually like, PEOPLE. And the strive to the top is like, our struggle in life. And like, being a butterfly is..." etc. The illustrations were cutesie pie though. This is such a hippie book I don't even know what else to say. It's hard to hate on such cheesy idealism.... I felt like I should be more impressed by the cute, universal message, than I was. Maybe it'd help if I was less cynical. Though I did like the "caterpillar pilar". Overall.. the drawings saved an otherwise cliche story. Oh, 70's. </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7780308-maria-ella?shelf=most-loved">most-loved</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer335299490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2708149967108244185">This allegory is totally amazing! Good thing there's a free blog containing this short story. For those who wanted a free read, you may refer to <a href='http://www.daleanderson.ca/hopefortheflowers.htm' rel='nofollow noopener'>this link</a>.<br/><br/><b>Review and Reflections</b>:<br/><br/>I was spending my idle time in my office desk. Thinking of something short yet worthwhile to read. I've read some articles about CJ on Trial Drama, Lady Gaga Concert, and Jessica Sanchez's potential to win this season's AI. When I went to this site and a friend rated this five stars, I searched for the free text of this </span>
  <span id="freeText2708149967108244185" style="display:none">This allegory is totally amazing! Good thing there's a free blog containing this short story. For those who wanted a free read, you may refer to <a href="http://www.daleanderson.ca/hopefortheflowers.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">this link</a>.<br /><br /><b>Review and Reflections</b>:<br /><br />I was spending my idle time in my office desk. Thinking of something short yet worthwhile to read. I've read some articles about CJ on Trial Drama, Lady Gaga Concert, and Jessica Sanchez's potential to win this season's AI. When I went to this site and a friend rated this five stars, I searched for the free text of this book. <br /><br />The story started with <b>Mr. Stripe</b>, curious about the pile of caterpillars having the desire to reach the top. During his climb, <i>and in an unexpected moment</i>, he met <b>Ms. Yellow</b>. Both having no idea what lies ahead, they decided to spend time together in the meantime, being with each other and enjoying each other's company. Until one day, boredom came. Mr. Stripe desired <i>more</i>. And so Ms. Yellow <i>let go</i>, respecting his decision - and moving on.<br /><br />When circumstances led Ms. Yellow <i>into greater heights</i>, she searched for Mr. Stripe. She searched, found, then waited for Mr. Stripe to realize the desires of Ms. Yellow's heart. Then one day, <i>finally</i>, they became the hope for the flowers.<br /><br />I want to feel the moment when Mr. Stripe met Ms. Yellow. Ms. Yellow was weak and fragile then, yet Mr. Stripe decided to be with her side since being together means being stronger against any challenge. But what if one day, he feels the boredom? the monotony? What if he wants <i>more</i>? With this vulnerable heart, should I be able to let go and move on without him?<br /><br />And when I meet him in some distant future, broken and messed-up, will I be able to forgive and forget, and able to help him up?<br /><br />I may not know these things yet, but I hope one day when I become as <i>iridescent</i> as a butterfly - we would see each other, would help each other, and would be the next hope for these wonderful flowers. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2708149967108244185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2193536681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193536681" />
    <a title="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books"><img alt="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525361625p2/873807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193536681?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" href="/user/show/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books">Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780809117543" href="/book/show/937227.Hope_for_the_Flowers">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books?shelf=readwomen">readwomen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books?shelf=thumbs-down">thumbs-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193536681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14515800625616742358">I received this book as a gift, which I was grateful for, but I just couldn't get on board with it. So here's the thing: this book has been around for 45 years+. It's kind of a children's book, sort of a self-help book, is supposed to provide inspiration and touches on psychology. And that's exactly my problem with it. Paulus has tried to be so all encompassing that the book just falls flat. There are too many messages and her agenda is just too long.<br/><br/><i>Hope For The Flowers</i> is little bit about love</span>
  <span id="freeText14515800625616742358" style="display:none">I received this book as a gift, which I was grateful for, but I just couldn't get on board with it. So here's the thing: this book has been around for 45 years+. It's kind of a children's book, sort of a self-help book, is supposed to provide inspiration and touches on psychology. And that's exactly my problem with it. Paulus has tried to be so all encompassing that the book just falls flat. There are too many messages and her agenda is just too long.<br /><br /><i>Hope For The Flowers</i> is little bit about love, a little bit about revolution, a good bit about hope and a whole lot about life. It can be read from philosophical, religious or political points of view, making even the story a bit too ambitious, which sounds ironic when we are dealing with a sparse, simplistic book that is in Paulus's own handwriting.<br /><br />I don't deny that this book took a long time to put together or that it isn't filled with the author's hugely passionate views and feelings, but in Paulus's attempts to make it <i>everything</i>, she has left it lacking.<br /><br />A big no for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14515800625616742358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all?shelf=thinking-people-s-books">thinking-people-s-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784114092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15314753744522418696">Yes.<br/>This is one of those books that you bring yourself to. You will read it through the filter of your experiences, background, and core beliefs. What your core beliefs actually ARE may surprise you; your reaction to books like this may make ideas you didn't know you cherished leap out at you and say BOO!<br/><br/>This is a "Marmite book"--you will love it or hate it.<br/><br/>It can be taken a myriad of ways, and will. But the fault if any lies not within our stars, but in ourselves.<br/><br/>If it makes you happy, cherish </span>
  <span id="freeText15314753744522418696" style="display:none">Yes.<br />This is one of those books that you bring yourself to. You will read it through the filter of your experiences, background, and core beliefs. What your core beliefs actually ARE may surprise you; your reaction to books like this may make ideas you didn't know you cherished leap out at you and say BOO!<br /><br />This is a "Marmite book"--you will love it or hate it.<br /><br />It can be taken a myriad of ways, and will. But the fault if any lies not within our stars, but in ourselves.<br /><br />If it makes you happy, cherish that.<br />If it makes you extremely angry, ask yourself why.<br /><br />If it leaves you indifferent...oh dear.<br /><br />Ostensibly it is a children's book. Perhaps when it first came out, it was. Kids were being taught to think rather deeply in those days. Today, however, it would be a wise child who would "get it." <br />Or a wise adult.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer327859677115886685">I've first read this book when I was like ten. It's been how many years now, and I still think that it's fantastic.<br/><br/>This books is about the journey of two caterpillars, Stripe and Yellow, and the obstacles and problems that they faced before they both became butterflies.<br/><br/>The story is simple, but beautiful and realistic.   <span id="freeText327859677115886685" style="display:none">I've first read this book when I was like ten. It's about learning to give up and let go. How each ending offers a new beginning. It's about taking risks. And the desire to see something more.<br><br>The illustrations are really wonderful. <div id="review_1162715" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1162715" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82840-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465057364p2/82840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1162715?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/82840-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11458727170194061573">This book is deceptively simple. It's for anyone in a relationship, anyone who wonders "is there more to life?", anyone who is trying to personally grow and to find themselves. Does that leave anyone out? It's sort of like a therapy fable. It took about 30 minutes to read, and it's the kind of book that you keep in your bedstand to pull out whenever you need to remind yourself that growth hurts and change can be very scary.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16169524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16169524" />
    <a title="Elyse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/809260-elyse"><img alt="Elyse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442507593p2/809260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16169524?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse" href="/user/show/809260-elyse">Elyse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/809260-elyse?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/809260-elyse?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16169524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7909163096428083599"> My father actually gave me this book so it has special connotations for me through sentimentality. The simple story is spectacular and sweet; touching on concepts such as isolation, peer pressure, independence, fear of change, prejudice and many more...yes this little book really does all that. I've read it at least four times to my daughter and every time she can apply its simple storyline to what ever happens to be going on in her ever changing, ever growing life </span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer54868817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11478660612932825817">This was a required reading in my Religion 101 class in college in the early 80’s. I remember the plot – a caterpillar who went on top of other caterpillar trying to reach a certain height. I think it is a story of becoming somebody among the many who do not have dreams. It is very much the same message as Jonathan Livingston Seagull. The only difference is that these are caterpillars metamorphosing into nice butterflies while Jonathan is a seagull who learned how to be different by flying. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27052034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27052034" />
    <a title="Spudsie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1296189-spudsie"><img alt="Spudsie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1215572268p2/1296189.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27052034?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Spudsie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Spudsie" href="/user/show/1296189-spudsie">Spudsie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone seeking inspiration or struggling to figure out what's at the top</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27052034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11149395399134661187">Wow. I had almost forgotten about this book. I was trying to find room in my (seriously overcrowded) bookshelves for a book I had just finished reading and ran into this one tucked away—waiting patiently to be rediscovered.<br/><br/>The book itself is a beautifully written and delightfully illustrated allegory of a caterpillar named Spike and his companion Yellow. It tells of Spike’s struggle to find…..well……happiness. Or perhaps more accurately (as I’m learning), to choose happiness. <br/><br/>Since the book is on</span>
  <span id="freeText11149395399134661187" style="display:none">Wow. I had almost forgotten about this book. I was trying to find room in my (seriously overcrowded) bookshelves for a book I had just finished reading and ran into this one tucked away—waiting patiently to be rediscovered.<br /><br />The book itself is a beautifully written and delightfully illustrated allegory of a caterpillar named Spike and his companion Yellow. It tells of Spike’s struggle to find…..well……happiness. Or perhaps more accurately (as I’m learning), to choose happiness. <br /><br />Since the book is only 144 pages long (and most of the space is illustrations not writing) I won’t say much more about the actual story of the book. This book gets five stars for far more personal reasons.<br /><br />I discovered “Hope for the Flowers” back in the late 1980’s. I must have given a copy of it to some member of my immediately family and forgotten about it. About a decade later it found its way back to me. My father had gone through some very challenging times that made him even more introspective than he typically is. He found the book somewhere and it touched it soul in a meaningful way. That Christmas he sent a copy of “Hope for the Flowers” to each of his children along with a touching two page letter. It was very moving to read of how he saw so much of himself and his life in this allegory. And how it gave him (along with the flowers) hope.<br /><br />Now I find myself on a journey of my own. One that is challenging me to grow and stretch (even metamorphose) in ways that require me to take unexpected leaps of faith. To do things I didn’t even know I was capable of doing. I am fortunate in that I (like Yellow) have a coach/mentor to help me along the way. Someone to tell me I won’t get stuck in my cocoon. (Or chrysalis.) It seems an appropriate time for the book to reappear.<br /><br />Every time I’ve read this allegory I’ve gleaned something new and different from it. This time I’ve realized three things. First, I am reminded that God (or the Universe as my coach would say) sends and resends books, people and information our way when we are ready for it. <br /><br />Second, that it is easier to make major changes in your life when you have someone encouraging you. I cannot imagine how Spike was able to take the leap of faith to weave his cocoon/chrysalis when Yellow was not able to verbally communicate with him. How difficult his choice to change must have been without a cheerleader. <br /><br />Finally, for the first time I looked at the title of the book after reading it. “Hope for the Flowers.” Maybe I’m stretching the allegory a little….but I doubt the author will object. Without butterflies the flowers would be doomed—hopeless. (Yes, yes….I understand there are dozens of other flying insects that will pollinate flowers…..but not all of the flowers.) If the caterpillars are not willing to make a drastic change, the flowers have no hope. It is only by risking everything, by making themselves vulnerable to the unknown that they are able to change into the amazing butterflies they were meant to be. The butterflies who allow the flowers to have hope. So in turn, when I am willing to do the hard work, take the risks and change I will be able to bring hope to others. To allow others to be what they were meant to be. <br /><br />Wow. That’s quite a big message from such a small book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11149395399134661187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18469829" />
    <a title="Naomi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/331771-naomi"><img alt="Naomi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190310529p2/331771.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18469829?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi" href="/user/show/331771-naomi">Naomi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/331771-naomi?shelf=on-my-bookshelf">on-my-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18469829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer238259296460802723">My boyfriend gave me an old copy of this book that he was about to throw out. I kept it, but didn't read it. It was obvious from the pictures and the title that it was a "Flower Child" book, and I figured I'd read it eventually. <br/><br/>Now I have read it. The timing on reading this book is so strange because at this moment in my life I am EXACTLY like "Stripe", one of the caterpillers in this story. I know something in my life needs to change, and I'm making my way down the huge caterpiller pile to fin</span>
  <span id="freeText238259296460802723" style="display:none">My boyfriend gave me an old copy of this book that he was about to throw out. I kept it, but didn't read it. It was obvious from the pictures and the title that it was a "Flower Child" book, and I figured I'd read it eventually. <br /><br />Now I have read it. The timing on reading this book is so strange because at this moment in my life I am EXACTLY like "Stripe", one of the caterpillers in this story. I know something in my life needs to change, and I'm making my way down the huge caterpiller pile to find something better, but I am TERRIFIED of going into the cocoon and letting go of all I know. So, reading this book brought tears to my eyes and put a big smile on my face, inspiring me to do what is right for me, even if it is sort of scary to take the leap of faith and let go of the security that is also what is making me miserable. Yeah, life can be just about getting by and filling our basic needs,and life can be about doing what everyone else is doing to try and get ahead, or it can be More. The lesson is that you have to venture into the unkown sometimes in order to reach your full potential. And that no one said it would be easy, but that doesn't mean you shouldn't do it.<br /><br />If you don't have any idea what I'm talking about, just read this book. But seriously, this was one of those life-changing experiences for me, and it's a book that I will cherish for the rest of my life and read to my future children or puppies.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1033669242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1033669242" />
    <a title="Sumit Singla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18177815-sumit-singla"><img alt="Sumit Singla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503976056p2/18177815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1033669242?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sumit Singla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sumit Singla" href="/user/show/18177815-sumit-singla">Sumit Singla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18177815-sumit-singla?shelf=inspiring">inspiring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18177815-sumit-singla?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18177815-sumit-singla?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1033669242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9262073867269128866">One part <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull' title='Jonathan Livingston Seagull by Richard Bach' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</a> and another part <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince' title='The Little Prince by Antoine de Saint-Exupéry' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Little Prince</a>, this is a short, sweet fable with an important message. It doesn't preach and you are free to read it like a children's story or to draw meaning from it.<br/><br/>The story is about two caterpillars Stripe and Yellow, who are trying to climb up the 'caterpillar pillar', which is well... as the name suggests, a pillar of caterpillars. All the caterpillars are trying to crawl over each other and get to the top.<br/><br/>So, do our protagonists j</span>
  <span id="freeText9262073867269128866" style="display:none">One part <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Jonathan Livingston Seagull by Richard Bach" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Livingston Seagull</a> and another part <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="The Little Prince by Antoine de Saint-Exupéry" rel="nofollow noopener">The Little Prince</a>, this is a short, sweet fable with an important message. It doesn't preach and you are free to read it like a children's story or to draw meaning from it.<br /><br />The story is about two caterpillars Stripe and Yellow, who are trying to climb up the 'caterpillar pillar', which is well... as the name suggests, a pillar of caterpillars. All the caterpillars are trying to crawl over each other and get to the top.<br /><br />So, do our protagonists join the <s>rat</s> caterpillar race or do they become non-conformists?<br /><br />The book is a great allegory about the true purpose of life, the choices we make, and putting things into some kind of rational perspective. It is easy to get into the trap of 'trying to get to the top' and almost impossible to get out of it.<br /><br />The illustrations are simplistic, the story is straightforward. Really? Faith. Hope. Love. Inspiration. All these and more in equal measure. If it were up to me, I'd make this a part of the new hire orientation pack of every organization I know about.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9262073867269128866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ez5FEkUPsq0GAQeQ3hPVUJW4JyBNIK/cAnRJSHijrVQg8mIOHM9Yi4bTmKkLTGDf72dpIPo/WsRqQU9TVmMQog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wlvHYijNs35zOQ3vsUtSkCxEF2iguQZTBEeIecOq62eZl+B+cQ1ZWPPrktZkFOcfVptZaBem80tsco5i7WpWkQ==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText6673001821637545405" style="display:none">Trina Paulus is the author of Hope for the Flowers, a novel "for adults and others (including caterpillars who can read). She describes herself as an "advocate of organic farming, composting, holistic health and spiritual search." Paulus lives in Montclair, New Jersey and acts as the vice-president of the Cornucopia Network of New Jersey. Paulus' archives of 25 years of the New Jersey environmental movement will be archived at the North Jersey Heritage Center at Fairleigh Dickinson University.<br /><br /></span>
